# PathRef | Slate

`PathRef` objects keep a specific path in a document synced over time as new operations are applied to the editor. It is created using the `Editor.pathRef` method. You can access their property `current` at any time for the up-to-date `Path` value. When you no longer need to track this location, call `unref()` to free the resources. The `affinity` refers to the direction the `PathRef` will go when a user inserts content at the current position of the `Path`.

Copy

    interface PathRef {
      current: Path | null
      affinity: 'forward' | 'backward' | null
      unref(): Path | null
    }

*   [Instance methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#instance-methods)
    
*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#static-methods)
    
    *   [Transform methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#trasnform-methods)
        
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#instance-methods)

Instance methods


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#unref-greater-than-path-or-null)

`unref() => Path | null`

Free the resources used by the PathRef. This should be called when you no longer need to track the path. Returns the final path value before being unrefed, or null if the path was already invalid.

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#static-methods)

Static methods


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#transform-methods)

Transform methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#pathref.transform-ref-pathref-op-operation)

`PathRef.transform(ref: PathRef, op: Operation)`

Transform the path refs current value by an `op`. The editor calls this as needed, so normally you won't need to.

[PreviousPathchevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path)
[NextPointchevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/point)

Last updated 9 months ago

*   [Instance methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#instance-methods)
    
*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#static-methods)
    
*   [Transform methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref#transform-methods)

# Operation | v0.47 | Slate

An operation is the lowest-level description of a specific change to a part of Slate's value. They are designed to be collaborative-editing friendly.

All of the [`Commands`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/commands)
 methods result in operations being created and applied to a [`Value`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/value)
 They're accessible via the `editor.operations` property.

There are a handful of Slate operation types. The goal is to have the fewest possible types, while still maintaining the necessary semantics for collaborative editing to work.

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#properties)

Properties


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

See each operation separately below to see what they consist of.

Note that all operations have a `data` property which can be used to attach arbitrary data to the operation, just like the [`Node`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/node)
 models ([`Block`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/block)
, [`Inline`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/inline)
, etc).

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#text-operations)

Text Operations


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#insert_text)

`insert_text`

Copy

    {
      type: 'insert_text',
      path: List,
      offset: Number,
      text: String,
      marks: List,
      data: Map,
    }

Inserts a `text` string at `offset` into a text node at `path`, with optional `marks` to be applied to the inserted characters.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#remove_text)

`remove_text`

Removes a string of `text` at `offset` into a text node at `path`.

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#mark-operations)

Mark Operations


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#add_mark)

`add_mark`

Adds a `mark` to the text node at `path` starting at an `offset` and spanning `length` characters.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#remove_mark)

`remove_mark`

Removes a `mark` from a text node at `path` starting at an `offset` and spanning `length` characters.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#set_mark)

`set_mark`

Set new `newProperties` on any marks that match an existing `properties` mark in a text node at `path`, starting at an `offset` and spanning `length` characters.

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#node-operations)

Node Operations


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#insert_node)

`insert_node`

Insert a new `node` at `path`.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#merge_node)

`merge_node`

Merge the node at `path` with its previous sibling. The `position` refers to either the index in the child nodes of the previous sibling in the case of [`Block`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/block)
 or [`Inline`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/inline)
 nodes, and the index in the characters of the previous sibling in the case of [`Text`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/text)
 nodes. The `properties` object contains properties of the merged node in the event that the change is undone.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#move_node)

`move_node`

Move the node at `path` to a `newPath`.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#remove_node)

`remove_node`

Remove the node at `path`.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#set_node)

`set_node`

Set new `properties` on the node at `path`.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#split_node)

`split_node`

Split the node at `path` at `position`. The `position` refers to either the index in the child nodes in the case of [`Block`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/block)
 or [`Inline`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/inline)
 nodes, and the index in the characters in the case of [`Text`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/text)
 nodes. In the case of nested splits, `target` refers to the target path of the child split operation. The `properties` object contains properties that should be assigned to the new node created after the split operation is complete.

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#value-operations)

Value Operations


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#set_selection)

`set_selection`

Set new `properties` on the selection.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#set_value)

`set_value`

Set new `properties` on a value. Properties can contain `data` and `decorations`.

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#helpers)

Helpers


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#apply)

`apply`

`apply(value: Value, operation: Object) => Value`

Applies an `operation` to a `value` object.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/operation#invert)

`invert`

`invert(operation: Object) => Object`

Create an inverse operation that will undo the changes made by the original.

[PreviousNodechevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/node)
[NextPluginschevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/plugins)

Last updated 6 years ago

# Location Types | Slate

The `Location` interface is a union of the ways to refer to a specific location in a Slate document: paths, points or ranges. Methods will often accept a `Location` instead of requiring only a `Path`, `Point` or `Range`.

Copy

    type Location = Path | Point | Range

*   [Location](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/location)
    
*   [Path](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path)
    
*   [PathRef](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref)
    
*   [Point](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/point)
    
*   [PointEntry](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/point-entry)
    
*   [PointRef](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/point-ref)
    
*   [Range](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range)
    
*   [RangeRef](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range-ref)
    
*   [Span](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/span)
    

[PreviousTextchevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text)
[NextLocationchevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/location)

Last updated 3 years ago

---

# Element | Slate

`Element` objects are a type of `Node` in a Slate document that contain other `Element` nodes or `Text` nodes.

Copy

    interface Element {
      children: Node[]
    }

*   [Behavior Types](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#element-behavior-types)
    
    *   [Block vs. Inline](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#block-vs-inline)
        
    *   [Void vs Not Void](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#void-vs-not-void)
        
        *   [Rendering Void Elements](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#rendering-void-elements)
            
        
    
*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#static-methods)
    
    *   [Retrieval methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#retrieval-methods)
        
    *   [Check methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#check-methods)
        
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#element-behavior-types)

Element Behavior Types


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Element nodes behave differently depending on the [Slate editor's configuration](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/editor#schema-specific-instance-methods-to-override)
. An element can be:

*   "block" or "inline" as defined by `editor.isInline`
    
*   either "void" or "not void" as defined by `editor.isVoid`
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#block-vs.-inline)

Block vs. Inline

A "block" element can only be siblings with other "block" elements. An "inline" node can be siblings with `Text` nodes or other "inline" elements.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#void-vs-not-void)

Void vs Not Void

In a not "void" element, Slate handles the rendering of its `children` (e.g. in a paragraph where the `Text` and `Inline` children are rendered by Slate). In a "void" element, the `children` are rendered by the `Element`'s render code.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#voids-that-support-marks)

Voids That Support Marks

Some void elements are effectively stand-ins for text, such as with the [Mentionsarrow-up-right](https://www.slatejs.org/examples/mentions)
 example, where the mention element renders the character's name. Users might want to format Void elements like this with bold, or set their font and size, so `editor.markableVoid` tells Slate whether or not to apply Marks to the text children of void elements.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#rendering-void-elements)

Rendering Void Elements

Void Elements must

*   always have one empty child text node (for selection)
    
*   render using `attributes` and `children` (so, their outermost HTML element **can't** be an HTML void element)
    
*   set `contentEditable={false}` (for Firefox)
    

Typical rendering code will resemble this `thematic-break` (horizontal rule) element:

For a "markable" void such as a `mention` element, marks on the empty child element can be used to determine how the void element is rendered (Slate Marks are applied only to Text leaves):

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#static-methods)

Static methods


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#retrieval-methods)

Retrieval methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#element.matches-element-element-props-partial-less-than-element-greater-than-greater-than-boolean)

`Element.matches(element: Element, props: Partial<Element>) => boolean`

Check if an element matches a set of `props`. Note: This checks custom properties, but it does not ensure that any children are equivalent.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#check-methods)

Check methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#element.isancestor-value-any-greater-than-value-is-ancestor)

`Element.isAncestor(value: any) => value is Ancestor`

Check if a value implements the 'Ancestor' interface.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#element.iselement-value-any-greater-than-value-is-element)

`Element.isElement(value: any) => value is Element`

Check if a `value` implements the `Element` interface.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#element.iselementlist-value-any-greater-than-value-is-element)

`Element.isElementList(value: any) => value is Element[]`

Check if a `value` is an array of `Element` objects.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#element.iselementtype-less-than-t-extends-element-greater-than-value-any-elementval-string-elementke)

`Element.isElementType<T Extends Element>(value: any, elementVal: string, ElementKey: string = 'type'): value is T`

Check if a value implements the `Element` interface and has elementKey with selected value. Default it check to `type` key value

[PreviousEditorchevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/editor)
[NextNodechevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node)

Last updated 3 years ago

*   [Element Behavior Types](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#element-behavior-types)
    
*   [Block vs. Inline](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#block-vs.-inline)
    
*   [Void vs Not Void](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#void-vs-not-void)
    
*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#static-methods)
    
*   [Retrieval methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#retrieval-methods)
    
*   [Check methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element#check-methods)
    

Copy

    return (
      <div {...attributes} contentEditable={false}>
        {children}
        <hr />
      </div>
    )

Copy

    const Mention = ({ attributes, children, element }) => {
      const selected = useSelected()
      const focused = useFocused()
      const style: React.CSSProperties = {
        padding: '3px 3px 2px',
        margin: '0 1px',
        verticalAlign: 'baseline',
        display: 'inline-block',
        borderRadius: '4px',
        backgroundColor: '#eee',
        fontSize: '0.9em',
        boxShadow: selected && focused ? '0 0 0 2px #B4D5FF' : 'none',
      }
      // See if our empty text child has any styling marks applied and apply those
      if (element.children[0].bold) {
        style.fontWeight = 'bold'
      }
      if (element.children[0].italic) {
        style.fontStyle = 'italic'
      }
      return (
        <span
          {...attributes}
          contentEditable={false}
          data-cy={`mention-${element.character.replace(' ', '-')}`}
          style={style}
        >
          {children}@{element.character}
        </span>
      )
    }

---

# Range | Slate

`Range` objects are a set of points that refer to a specific span of a Slate document. They can define a span inside a single node or they can span across multiple nodes. The editor's `selection` is stored as a range.

Copy

    interface Range {
      anchor: Point
      focus: Point
    }

*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#static-methods)
    
    *   [Retrieval methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#retrieval-methods)
        
    *   [Check methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#check-methods)
        
    *   [Transform methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#transform-methods)
        
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#static-methods)

Static methods


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#retrieval-methods)

Retrieval methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.edges-range-range-options-greater-than-point-point)

`Range.edges(range: Range, options?) => [Point, Point]`

Get the start and end points of a `range`, in the order in which they appear in the document.

Options: `{reverse?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.end-range-range-greater-than-point)

`Range.end(range: Range) => Point`

Get the end point of a `range` according to the order in which it appears in the document.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.intersection-range-range-another-range-greater-than-range-or-null)

`Range.intersection(range: Range, another: Range) => Range | null`

Get the intersection of one `range` with `another`. If the two ranges do not overlap, return `null`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.points-range-range-greater-than-generator-less-than-pointentry-greater-than)

`Range.points(range: Range) => Generator<PointEntry>`

Iterate through the two point entries in a `Range`. First it will yield a `PointEntry` representing the `anchor`, then it will yield a `PointEntry` representing the `focus`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.start-range-range-greater-than-point)

`Range.start(range: Range) => Point`

Get the start point of a `range` according to the order in which it appears in the document.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#check-methods)

Check methods

Check some attribute of a Range. Always returns a boolean.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.equals-range-range-another-range-greater-than-boolean)

`Range.equals(range: Range, another: Range) => boolean`

Check if a `range` is exactly equal to `another`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.includes-range-range-target-path-or-point-or-range-greater-than-boolean)

`Range.includes(range: Range, target: Path | Point | Range) => boolean`

Check if a `range` includes a path, a point, or part of another range.

For clarity the definition of `includes` can mean partially includes. Another way to describe this is if one Range intersects the other Range.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.surrounds-range-range-target-range-greater-than-boolean)

`Range.surrounds(range: Range, target: Range) => boolean`

Check if a `range` includes another range.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.isbackward-range-range-greater-than-boolean)

`Range.isBackward(range: Range) => boolean`

Check if a `range` is backward, meaning that its anchor point appears _after_ its focus point in the document.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.iscollapsed-range-range-greater-than-boolean)

`Range.isCollapsed(range: Range) => boolean`

Check if a `range` is collapsed, meaning that both its anchor and focus points refer to the exact same position in the document.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.isexpanded-range-range-greater-than-boolean)

`Range.isExpanded(range: Range) => boolean`

Check if a `range` is expanded. This is the opposite of `Range.isCollapsed` and is provided for legibility.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.isforward-range-range-greater-than-boolean)

`Range.isForward(range: Range) => boolean`

Check if a `range` is forward. This is the opposite of `Range.isBackward` and is provided for legibility.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.isrange-value-any-greater-than-value-is-range)

`Range.isRange(value: any) => value is Range`

Check if a `value` implements the `Range` interface.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#transform-methods)

Transform methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/range#range.transform-range-range-op-operation-options-greater-than-range-or-null)

`Range.transform(range: Range, op: Operation, options) => Range | null`

Transform a `range` by an `op`.

Options: `{affinity: 'forward' | 'backward' | 'outward' | 'inward' | null}`

# Hooks | Slate

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#usecomposing-boolean)

`useComposing(): boolean`

Get the current `composing` state of the editor. It deals with `compositionstart`, `compositionupdate`, `compositionend` events.

Composition events are triggered by typing (composing) with a language that uses a composition character (e.g. Chinese, Japanese, Korean, etc.) [examplearrow-up-right](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Input_method#/media/File:Typing_%EC%9E%88%EC%8A%B5%EB%8B%88%EB%8B%A4_in_Dubeolsik_keyboard_layout.gif)
.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#useelement-element)

`useElement(): Element`

Get the current element object. Re-renders whenever the element or any of its descendants changes.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#useelementif-element-or-null)

`useElementIf(): Element | null`

The same as `useElement()` but returns `null` instead of throwing an error when not inside an element.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#usefocused-boolean)

`useFocused(): boolean`

Get the current `focused` state of the editor.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#usereadonly-boolean)

`useReadOnly(): boolean`

Get the current `readOnly` state of the editor.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#useselected-boolean)

`useSelected(): boolean`

Get the current `selected` state of an element. An element is selected if `editor.selection` exists and overlaps any part of the element.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#useslate-editor)

`useSlate(): Editor`

Get the current editor object. Re-renders whenever changes occur in the editor.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#useslatestatic-editor)

`useSlateStatic(): Editor`

Get the current editor object from the React context. A version of useSlate that does not re-render the context. Previously called `useEditor`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#useslateselection-baserange-and-placeholder-string-or-undefined-onplaceholderresize-node-htmlelement)

`useSlateSelection(): (BaseRange & { placeholder?: string | undefined; onPlaceholderResize?: ((node: HTMLElement | null) => void) | undefined }) | null`

Get the current editor selection. Only re-renders when the selection changes.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks#useslateselector-less-than-t-greater-than-selector-editor-editor-greater-than-t-equalityfn-a-t-b-t-g)

`useSlateSelector<T>(selector: (editor: Editor) => T, equalityFn?: (a: T, b: T) => boolean): T`

Use redux style selectors to prevent re-rendering on every keystroke.

Bear in mind re-rendering can only prevented if the returned value is a value type or for reference types (e.g. objects and arrays) add a custom equality function.

If `selector` is memoized using `useCallback`, then it will only be called when it or the editor state changes. Otherwise, `selector` will be called every time the component renders.

Example:

[PreviousReactEditorchevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/react-editor)
[NextSlate Componentchevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate)

Last updated 7 months ago

Copy

    const isSelectionActive = useSlateSelector(editor => Boolean(editor.selection))

---

# Text | Slate

`Text` objects represent the nodes that contain the actual text content of a Slate document along with any formatting properties. They are always leaf nodes in the document tree as they cannot contain any children.

Copy

    interface Text {
      text: string
    }

*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#static-methods)
    
    *   [Retrieval methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#retrieval-methods)
        
    *   [Check methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#check-methods)
        
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#static-methods)

Static methods


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#retrieval-methods)

Retrieval methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#text.matches-text-text-props-partial-less-than-text-greater-than-greater-than-boolean)

`Text.matches(text: Text, props: Partial<Text>) => boolean`

Check if `text` matches a set of `props`.

The way the check works is that it makes sure that (a) all the `props` exist in the `text`, and (b) if it exists, that it exactly matches the properties in the `text`.

If a `props.text` property is passed in, it will be ignored.

If there are properties in `text` that are not in `props`, those will be ignored when it comes to testing for a match.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#text.decorations-node-text-decorations-decoratedrange-greater-than-leaf-text-position-leafposition)

`Text.decorations(node: Text, decorations: DecoratedRange[]) => { leaf: Text; position?: LeafPosition }[]`

Get the leaves and positions for a text node, given `decorations`.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#check-methods)

Check methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#text.equals-text-text-another-text-options-greater-than-boolean)

`Text.equals(text: Text, another: Text, options?) => boolean`

Check if two text nodes are equal.

Options: `{loose?: boolean}`

*   `loose?`: When `true`, it checks if the properties of the `Text` object are equal except for the `text` property (i.e. the `String` value of the `Text`). When `false` (default), checks all properties including `text`.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#text.istext-value-any-greater-than-value-is-text)

`Text.isText(value: any) => value is Text`

Check if a `value` implements the `Text` interface.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#text.istextlist-value-any-value-is-text)

`Text.isTextList(value: any): value is Text[]`

Check if `value` is an `Array` of only `Text` objects.

[PreviousNodeEntrychevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node-entry)
[NextLocation Typeschevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations)

Last updated 9 months ago

*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#static-methods)
    
*   [Retrieval methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#retrieval-methods)
    
*   [Check methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/text#check-methods)

# Slate Component | Slate

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate#slate-props-slateprops-react.jsx.element)

`Slate(props: SlateProps): React.JSX.Element`


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `Slate` component must include somewhere in its `children` the `Editable` component.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate#props)

Props

Copy

    type SlateProps = {
      editor: ReactEditor
      value: Descendant[]
      children: React.ReactNode
      onChange?: (value: Descendant[]) => void
      onSelectionChange?: (selection: Selection) => void
      onValueChange?: (value: Descendant[]) => void
    }

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate#props.editor-reacteditor)

`props.editor: ReactEditor`

An instance of `ReactEditor`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate#props.value-descendant)

`props.value: Descendant[]`

The initial value of the Editor.

This prop is deceptively named.

Slate once was a controlled component (i.e. it's contents were strictly controlled by the `value` prop) but due to features like its edit history which would be corrupted by direct editing of the `value` it is no longer a controlled component.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate#props.children-react.reactnode)

`props.children: React.ReactNode`

The `children` which must contain an `Editable` component.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate#props.onchange-value-descendant-greater-than-void)

`props.onChange: (value: Descendant[]) => void`

An optional callback function which you can use to be notified of changes in the editor's value.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate#props.onvaluechange-value-descendant-greater-than-void)

`props.onValueChange?: (value: Descendant[]) => void`

`props.onChange` alias.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate#props.onselectionchange-selection-selection-greater-than-void)

`props.onSelectionChange?: (selection: Selection) => void`

An optional callback function which you can use to be notified of changes of the editor's selection.

[PreviousHookschevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/hooks)
[NextEditable Componentchevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/editable)

Last updated 27 days ago

*   [Props](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/slate#props)

# Path | Slate

`Path` arrays are a list of indexes that describe a node's exact position in a Slate node tree. Although they are usually relative to the root `Editor` object, they can be relative to any `Node` object.

Copy

    type Path = number[]

*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#static-methods)
    
    *   [Retrieval methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#retrieval-methods)
        
    *   [Check methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#check-methods)
        
    *   [Transform method](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#transform-method)
        
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#static-methods)

Static methods


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#retrieval-methods)

Retrieval methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.ancestors-path-path-options-reverse-boolean-greater-than-path)

`Path.ancestors(path: Path, options: { reverse?: boolean } = {}) => Path[]`

Get a list of ancestor paths for a given path.

The paths are sorted from shallowest to deepest ancestor. However, if the `reverse: true` option is passed, they are reversed.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.common-path-path-another-path-greater-than-path)

`Path.common(path: Path, another: Path) => Path`

Get the common ancestor path of two paths.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.compare-path-path-another-path-greater-than-1-or-0-or-1)

`Path.compare(path: Path, another: Path) => -1 | 0 | 1`

Compare a path to another, returning an integer indicating whether the path was before, at, or after the other.

Note: Two paths of unequal length can still receive a `0` result if one is directly above or below the other. If you want exact matching, use \[\[Path.equals\]\] instead.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.levels-path-path-options-greater-than-path)

`Path.levels(path: Path, options?) => Path[]`

Get a list of paths at every level down to a path. Note: this is the same as `Path.ancestors`, but includes the path itself.

The paths are sorted from shallowest to deepest. However, if the `reverse: true` option is passed, they are reversed.

Options: `{reverse?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.next-path-path-greater-than-path)

`Path.next(path: Path) => Path`

Given a path, gets the path to the next sibling node. The method does not ensure that the returned `Path` is valid in the document.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.parent-path-path-greater-than-path)

`Path.parent(path: Path) => Path`

Given a path, return a new path referring to the parent node above it. If the `path` argument is equal to `[]`, throws an error.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.previous-path-path-greater-than-path)

`Path.previous(path: Path) => Path`

Given a path, get the path to the previous sibling node. The method will throw an error if there are no previous siblings (e.g. if the Path is currently `[1, 0]`, the previous path would be `[1, -1]` which is illegal and will throw an error).

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.relative-path-path-ancestor-path-greater-than-path)

`Path.relative(path: Path, ancestor: Path) => Path`

Given two paths, one that is an ancestor to the other, returns the relative path from the `ancestor` argument to the `path` argument. If the `ancestor` path is not actually an ancestor or equal to the `path` argument, throws an error.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#check-methods)

Check methods

Check some attribute of a path. Always returns a boolean.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.endsafter-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.endsAfter(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path ends after one of the indexes in another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.endsat-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.endsAt(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path ends at one of the indexes in another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.endsbefore-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.endsBefore(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path ends before one of the indexes in another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.equals-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.equals(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path is exactly equal to another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.hasprevious-path-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.hasPrevious(path: Path) => boolean`

Check if the path of previous sibling node exists

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.isafter-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.isAfter(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path is after another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.isancestor-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.isAncestor(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path is an ancestor of another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.isbefore-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.isBefore(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path is before another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.ischild-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.isChild(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path is a child of another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.iscommon-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.isCommon(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path is equal to or an ancestor of another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.isdescendant-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.isDescendant(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path is a descendant of another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.isparent-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.isParent(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path is the parent of another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.ispath-value-any-greater-than-value-is-path)

`Path.isPath(value: any) => value is Path`

Check is a value implements the `Path` interface.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.issibling-path-path-another-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Path.isSibling(path: Path, another: Path) => boolean`

Check if a path is a sibling of another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.operationcantransformpath-operation-operation-greater-than-operation-is-insertnodeoperation-or)

`Path.operationCanTransformPath(operation: Operation) => operation is InsertNodeOperation | RemoveNodeOperation | MergeNodeOperation | SplitNodeOperation | MoveNodeOperation`

Returns whether this operation can affect paths or not.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#transform-method)

Transform method

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path#path.transform-path-path-operation-operation-options-greater-than-path-or-null)

`Path.transform(path: Path, operation: Operation, options?) => Path | null`

Transform a path by an operation.

Options: `{ affinity?: 'forward' | 'backward' | null }`

[PreviousLocationchevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/location)
[NextPathRefchevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/locations/path-ref)

Last updated 9 months ago

# HistoryEditor | Slate

The `HistoryEditor` interface is added to the `Editor` when it is instantiated using the `withHistory` method.

Copy

    const [editor] = useState(() => withReact(withHistory(createEditor())))

This adds properties to `editor` that enables undo and redo in Slate.

There are also static methods for working with the Editor's undo/redo history.

Copy

    export interface HistoryEditor extends BaseEditor {
      history: History
      undo: () => void
      redo: () => void
      writeHistory: (stack: 'undos' | 'redos', batch: any) => void
    }

*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#static-methods)
    
    *   [Undo and Redo](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#undo-and-redo)
        
    *   [Merging and Saving](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#merging-and-saving)
        
    *   [Check methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#check-methods)
        
    
*   [Instance methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#instance-methods)
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#static-methods)

Static methods


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#undo-and-redo)

Undo and Redo

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#historyeditor.redo-editor-historyeditor-void)

`HistoryEditor.redo(editor: HistoryEditor): void`

Redo to the next saved state.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#historyeditor.undo-editor-historyeditor-void)

`HistoryEditor.undo(editor: HistoryEditor): void`

Undo to the previous saved state.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#merging-and-saving)

Merging and Saving

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#historyeditor.withmerging-editor-historyeditor-fn-greater-than-void-void)

`HistoryEditor.withMerging(editor: HistoryEditor, fn: () => void): void`

Apply a series of changes inside a synchronous `fn`, These operations will be merged into the previous history.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#historyeditor.withnewbatch-editor-historyeditor-fn-greater-than-void-void)

`HistoryEditor.withNewBatch(editor: HistoryEditor, fn: () => void): void`

Apply a series of changes inside a synchronous `fn`, ensuring that the first operation starts a new batch in the history. Subsequent operations will be merged as usual.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#historyeditor.withoutmerging-editor-historyeditor-fn-greater-than-void-void)

`HistoryEditor.withoutMerging(editor: HistoryEditor, fn: () => void): void`

Apply a series of changes inside a synchronous `fn`, without merging any of the new operations into previous save point in the history.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#historyeditor.withoutsaving-editor-historyeditor-fn-greater-than-void-void)

`HistoryEditor.withoutSaving(editor: HistoryEditor, fn: () => void): void`

Apply a series of changes inside a synchronous `fn`, without saving any of their operations into the history.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#check-methods)

Check methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#historyeditor.ishistoryeditor-value-any-value-is-historyeditor)

`HistoryEditor.isHistoryEditor(value: any): value is HistoryEditor`

Check if a value is a `HistoryEditor` (i.e. it has the `HistoryEditor` interface).

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#historyeditor.ismerging-editor-historyeditor-boolean-or-undefined)

`HistoryEditor.isMerging(editor: HistoryEditor): boolean | undefined`

Get the merge flag's current value.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#historyeditor.issaving-editor-historyeditor-boolean-or-undefined)

`HistoryEditor.isSaving(editor: HistoryEditor): boolean | undefined`

Get the saving flag's current value.

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#instance-methods)

Instance methods


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#undo-void)

`undo(): void`

Undo the last batch of operations

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#redo-void)

`redo(): void`

Redo the last undone batch of operations

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-history/history-editor#writehistory-stack-undos-or-redos-batch-any-greater-than-void)

`writeHistory(stack: 'undos'| 'redos', batch: any) => void`

Push a batch of operations as either `undos` or `redos` onto `editor.undos` or `editor.redos`

# ReactEditor | Slate

`ReactEditor` is added to `Editor` when it is instantiated using the `withReact` method.

Copy

    const [editor] = useState(() => withReact(withHistory(createEditor())))

*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/react-editor#static-methods)
    
    *   [Check methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/react-editor#check-methods)
        
    *   [Focus and selection methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/react-editor#focus-and-selection-methods)
        
    *   [DOM translation methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/react-editor#dom-translation-methods)
        
    *   [DataTransfer methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/react-editor#datatransfer-methods)
        
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/libraries/slate-react/react-editor#static-methods)

# Plugins | v0.47 | Slate

Plugins can be attached to an editor to alter its behavior in different ways. Each editor has a "stack" of plugins, which has a specific order, which it runs through when certain hooks are triggered.

Plugins are plain JavaScript objects, containing a set of middleware functions that run for each hook they choose to implement.

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#hooks)

Hooks


------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In addition to the [core plugin hooks](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-core/plugins)
, when using `slate-react` there are additional browser-specific event handling hooks, and React-specific rendering hooks available to plugins.

Copy

    {
      decorateNode: Function,
      onBeforeInput: Function,
      onBlur: Function,
      onCopy: Function,
      onCut: Function,
      onDrop: Function,
      onFocus: Function,
      onKeyDown: Function,
      onKeyUp: Function,
      onMouseUp: Function,
      onPaste: Function,
      onSelect: Function,
      renderEditor: Function,
      renderMark: Function,
      renderAnnotation: Function,
      renderDecoration: Function,
      renderBlock: Function,
      renderInline: Function,
      shouldNodeComponentUpdate: Function,
    }

The event hooks have a signature of `(event, editor, next)`ŌĆöthe `event` is a React object that you are used to from React's event handlers.

The rendering hooks are just like render props common to other React API's, and receive `(props, editor, next)`. For more information, see the [Rendering](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/rendering)
 reference.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#decoratenode)

`decorateNode`

`Function decorateNode(node: Node, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Array<Decoration>|Void`

The `decorateNode` hook takes a `node` and returns an array of decorations with marks to be applied to the node when it is rendered.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#onbeforeinput)

`onBeforeInput`

`Function onBeforeInput(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is called right before a string of text is inserted into the `contenteditable` element.

Make sure to `event.preventDefault()` if you do not want the default insertion behavior to occur!

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#onblur)

`onBlur`

`Function onBlur(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is called when the editor's `contenteditable` element is blurred.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#onfocus)

`onFocus`

`Function onFocus(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is called when the editor's `contenteditable` element is focused.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#oncopy)

`onCopy`

`Function onCopy(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is called when there is a copy event in the editor's `contenteditable` element.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#oncut)

`onCut`

`Function onCut(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is equivalent to the `onCopy` handler.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#ondrop)

`onDrop`

`Function onDrop(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is called when the user drops content into the `contenteditable` element. The event is already prevented by default, so you must define a value change to have any affect occur.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#onkeydown)

`onKeyDown`

`Function onKeyDown(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is called when any key is pressed in the `contenteditable` element, before any action is taken.

Make sure to `event.preventDefault()` if you do not want the default insertion behavior to occur!

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#onkeyup)

`onKeyUp`

`Function onKeyUp(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is called when any key is released in the `contenteditable` element.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#onpaste)

`onPaste`

`Function onPaste(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is called when the user pastes content into the `contenteditable` element. The event is already prevented by default, so you must define a value change to have any affect occur.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#onselect)

`onSelect`

`Function onSelect(event: Event, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean`

This handler is called whenever the native DOM selection changes.

> ­¤ż¢ This is **not** Slate's internal selection representation. If you want to get notified when Slate's `value.selection` changes, use the [`onChange`](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/editor#onchange)
>  property of the `<Editor>`. This handler is instead meant to give you lower-level access to the DOM selection handling, which **is not always triggered** as you'd expect.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#rendereditor)

`renderEditor`

`Function renderEditor(props: Object, editor: Editor, next: Function) => ReactNode|Void`

The `renderEditor` property allows you to define higher-order-component-like behavior. It is passed all of the properties of the editor, including `children`, which you can access as `next()`. You can then choose to wrap the existing `children` in any custom elements or proxy the properties however you choose. Note, that multiple plugins can define `renderEditor` and each one can add a specific behaviour to the editor, as `next()` refers to `children` from another plugin in the stack. This can be useful for rendering toolbars, styling the editor, rendering validation, etc, and each plugin can be responsible for a given functionality only, keeping your code dry and well organized. Just remember that the `renderEditor` function has to render `children` for editor's content to render. For example:

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#rendermark)

`renderMark`

`Function renderMark(props: Object, editor: Editor, next: Function) => ReactNode|Void`

Render a `Mark` with `props`. The `props` object contains:

You must spread the `props.attributes` onto the top-level DOM node you use to render the mark.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#renderdecoration)

`renderDecoration`

`Function renderDecoration(props: Object, editor: Editor, next: Function) => ReactNode|Void`

Render a `Decoration` with `props`. The `props` object contains:

You must spread the `props.attributes` onto the top-level DOM node you use to render the annotation.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#renderannotation)

`renderAnnotation`

`Function renderAnnotation(props: Object, editor: Editor, next: Function) => ReactNode|Void`

Render an `Annotation` with `props`. The `props` object contains:

You must spread the `props.attributes` onto the top-level DOM node you use to render the annotation.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#renderblock)

`renderBlock`

`Function renderBlock(props: Object, editor: Editor, next: Function) => ReactNode|Void`

Render a Block `Node` with `props`. The `props` object contains:

You must spread the `props.attributes` onto the top-level DOM node you use to render the node. You must also be sure to assign `attributes.ref` to the native DOM component being rendered (using `forwardRef` or `innerRef` if necessary).

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#renderinline)

`renderInline`

`Function renderInline(props: Object, editor: Editor, next: Function) => ReactNode|Void`

Render an Inline `Node` with `props`. The `props` object contains:

You must spread the `props.attributes` onto the top-level DOM node you use to render the node. You must also be sure to assign `attributes.ref` to the native DOM component being rendered (using `forwardRef` or `innerRef` if necessary).

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/plugins#shouldnodecomponentupdate)

`shouldNodeComponentUpdate`

`Function shouldNodeComponentUpdate(previousProps: Object, props: Object, editor: Editor, next: Function) => Boolean|Void`

If this function returns `true`, it can force updating the node's component where otherwise it wouldn't for performance.

[PreviousEditorchevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/editor)
[NextRenderingchevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/v0.47/slate-react/rendering)

Last updated 6 years ago

    renderEditor: (props, editor, next) => {

        <div>
          <MyToolbarComponent editor={editor} />

        </div>
      )
    }

# Transforms | Slate

Transforms are helper functions operating on the document. They can be used in defining your own commands.

*   [Node options](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#node-options)
    
*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#static-methods)
    
    *   [Node transforms](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#node-transforms)
        
    *   [Selection transforms](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#selection-transforms)
        
    *   [Text transforms](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#text-transforms)
        
    *   [Editor transforms](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#editor-transforms)
        
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#node-options)

Node options


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All transforms support a parameter `options`. This includes options specific to the transform and general `NodeOptions` to specify which Nodes in the document the transform is applied to.

Copy

    interface NodeOptions {
      at?: Location
      match?: (node: Node, path: Location) => boolean
      mode?: 'highest' | 'lowest'
      voids?: boolean
    }

*   The `at` option selects a [Location](https://docs.slatejs.org/concepts/03-locations)
     in the editor. It defaults to the user's current selection. [Learn more about the `at` option](https://docs.slatejs.org/concepts/04-transforms#the-at-option)
    
*   The `match` option filters the set of Nodes with a custom function. [Learn more about the `match` option](https://docs.slatejs.org/concepts/04-transforms#the-match-option)
    
*   The `mode` option also filters the set of nodes.
    
*   When `voids` is false, [void Elements](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/editor#schema-specific-instance-methods-to-override)
     are filtered out.
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#static-methods)

Static methods


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#node-transforms)

Node transforms

These transforms operate on nodes.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.insertfragment-editor-editor-fragment-node-options)

`Transforms.insertFragment(editor: Editor, fragment: Node[], options?)`

Insert a fragment of nodes at the specified location or (if not defined) the current selection or (if not defined) the end of the document.

Options: `{at?: Location, hanging?: boolean, voids?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.insertnodes-editor-editor-nodes-node-or-node-options)

`Transforms.insertNodes(editor: Editor, nodes: Node | Node[], options?)`

Atomically inserts `nodes` at the specified location or (if not defined) the current selection or (if not defined) the end of the document.

Options supported: `NodeOptions & {hanging?: boolean, select?: boolean}`.

For example, to insert at the very end, without replacing the current selection and regardless of block nesting, use

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.removenodes-editor-editor-options)

`Transforms.removeNodes(editor: Editor, options?)`

Remove nodes at the specified location in the document. If no location is specified, remove the nodes in the selection.

Options supported: `NodeOptions & {hanging?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.mergenodes-editor-editor-options)

`Transforms.mergeNodes(editor: Editor, options?)`

Merge a node at the specified location with the previous node at the same depth. If no location is specified, use the selection. Resulting empty container nodes are removed.

Options supported: `NodeOptions & {hanging?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.splitnodes-editor-editor-options)

`Transforms.splitNodes(editor: Editor, options?)`

Split nodes at the specified location. If no location is specified, split the selection.

Options supported: `NodeOptions & {height?: number, always?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.wrapnodes-editor-editor-element-element-options)

`Transforms.wrapNodes(editor: Editor, element: Element, options?)`

Wrap nodes at the specified location in the `element` container. If no location is specified, wrap the selection.

Options supported: `NodeOptions & {split?: boolean}`.

*   `options.mode`: `'all'` is also supported.
    
*   `options.split` indicates that it's okay to split a node in order to wrap the location. For example, if `ipsum` was selected in a `Text` node with `lorem ipsum dolar`, `split: true` would wrap the word `ipsum` only, resulting in splitting the `Text` node. If `split: false`, the entire `Text` node `lorem ipsum dolar` would be wrapped.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.unwrapnodes-editor-editor-options)

`Transforms.unwrapNodes(editor: Editor, options?)`

Unwrap nodes at the specified location. If necessary, the parent node is split. If no location is specified, use the selection.

Options supported: `NodeOptions & {split?: boolean}`. For `options.mode`, `'all'` is also supported.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.setnodes-editor-editor-props-partial-less-than-node-greater-than-options)

`Transforms.setNodes(editor: Editor, props: Partial<Node>, options?)`

Set properties of nodes at the specified location. If no location is specified, use the selection.

If `props` contains `undefined` values, the node's corresponding property will also be set to `undefined` as opposed to ignored.

Options supported: `NodeOptions & {hanging?: boolean, split?: boolean}`. For `options.mode`, `'all'` is also supported.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.unsetnodes-editor-editor-props-string-or-string-options)

`Transforms.unsetNodes(editor: Editor, props: string | string[], options?)`

Unset properties of nodes at the specified location. If no location is specified, use the selection.

Options supported: `NodeOptions & {hanging?: boolean, split?: boolean}`. For `options.mode`, `'all'` is also supported.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.liftnodes-editor-editor-options)

`Transforms.liftNodes(editor: Editor, options?)`

Lift nodes at the specified location upwards in the document tree. If necessary, the parent node is split. If no location is specified, use the selection.

Options supported: `NodeOptions`. For `options.mode`, `'all'` is also supported.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.movenodes-editor-editor-options)

`Transforms.moveNodes(editor: Editor, options)`

Move the nodes from an origin to a destination. A destination must be specified in the `options`. If no origin is specified, move the selection.

Options supported: `NodeOptions & {to: Path}`. For `options.mode`, `'all'` is also supported.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#selection-transforms)

Selection transforms

Transforms that operate on the document's selection.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.collapse-editor-editor-options)

`Transforms.collapse(editor: Editor, options?)`

Collapse the selection to a single point.

Options: `{edge?: 'anchor' | 'focus' | 'start' | 'end'}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.select-editor-editor-target-location)

`Transforms.select(editor: Editor, target: Location)`

Set the selection to a new value specified by `target`. When a selection already exists, this method is just a proxy for `setSelection` and will update the existing value.

For example, to set the selection to the entire contents of the editor:

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.deselect-editor-editor)

`Transforms.deselect(editor: Editor)`

Unset the selection.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.move-editor-editor-options)

`Transforms.move(editor: Editor, options?)`

Move the selection's point forward or backward.

Options: `{distance?: number, unit?: 'offset' | 'character' | 'word' | 'line', reverse?: boolean, edge?: 'anchor' | 'focus' | 'start' | 'end'}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.setpoint-editor-editor-props-partial-less-than-point-greater-than-options)

`Transforms.setPoint(editor: Editor, props: Partial<Point>, options?)`

Set new properties on one of the selection's points.

Options: `{edge?: 'anchor' | 'focus' | 'start' | 'end'}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.setselection-editor-editor-props-partial-less-than-range-greater-than)

`Transforms.setSelection(editor: Editor, props: Partial<Range>)`

Set new properties on an active selection. Since the value is a `Partial<Range>`, this method can only handle updates to an existing selection. If there is no active selection the operation will be void. Use `select` if you'd like to create a selection when there is none.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#text-transforms)

Text transforms

Transforms that operate on text.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.delete-editor-editor-options)

`Transforms.delete(editor: Editor, options?)`

Delete text in the document.

Options: `{at?: Location, distance?: number, unit?: 'character' | 'word' | 'line' | 'block', reverse?: boolean, hanging?: boolean, voids?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.inserttext-editor-editor-text-string-options)

`Transforms.insertText(editor: Editor, text: string, options?)`

Insert a string of text at the specified location or (if not defined) the current selection or (if not defined) the end of the document.

Options: `{at?: Location, voids?: boolean}`

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#editor-transforms)

Editor transforms

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/transforms#transforms.transform-editor-editor-transform-transform)

`Transforms.transform(editor: Editor, transform: Transform)`

Transform the `editor` by an `operation`.

[PreviousMigratingchevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/concepts/xx-migrating)
[NextNode Typeschevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes)

    Transforms.insertNodes(
      editor,
      { type: targetType, children: [{ text: '' }] },
      { at: [editor.children.length] }
    )

      anchor: Editor.start(editor, []),
      focus: Editor.end(editor, []),
    })

# Node | Slate

*   [Static methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#static-methods)
    
    *   [Retrieval methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#retrieval-methods)
        
    *   [Text methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#text-methods)
        
    *   [Check methods](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#check-methods)
        
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#static-methods)

Static methods


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#retrieval-methods)

Retrieval methods

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.ancestor-root-node-path-path-greater-than-ancestor)

`Node.ancestor(root: Node, path: Path) => Ancestor`

Get the node at a specific `path`, asserting that it is an ancestor node. If the specified node is not an ancestor node, throw an error.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.ancestors-root-node-path-path-options-greater-than-generator-less-than-nodeentry-less-than-ance)

`Node.ancestors(root: Node, path: Path, options?) => Generator<NodeEntry<Ancestor>>`

Return a generator of all the ancestor nodes above a specific path. By default, the order is top-down, from highest to lowest ancestor in the tree, but you can pass the `reverse: true` option to go bottom-up.

Options: `{reverse?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.child-root-node-index-number-greater-than-descendant)

`Node.child(root: Node, index: number) => Descendant`

Get the child of a node at the specified `index`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.children-root-node-path-path-options-greater-than-generator-less-than-nodeentry-less-than-desce)

`Node.children(root: Node, path: Path, options?) => Generator<NodeEntry<Descendant>>`

Iterate over the children of a node at a specific path.

Options: `{reverse?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.common-root-node-path-path-another-path-greater-than-nodeentry)

`Node.common(root: Node, path: Path, another: Path) => NodeEntry`

Get an entry for the common ancestor node of two paths. It might be a Text node, an Element, or the Editor itself.

For the common block ancestor, see [Editor Selectionarrow-up-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/concepts/03-locations#selection)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.descendant-root-node-path-path-greater-than-descendant)

`Node.descendant(root: Node, path: Path) => Descendant`

Get the node at a specific path, asserting that it's a descendant node.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.descendants-root-node-options-greater-than-generator-less-than-nodeentry-less-than-descendant-g)

`Node.descendants(root: Node, options?) => Generator<NodeEntry<Descendant>>`

Return a generator of all the descendant node entries inside a root node. Each iteration will return a `NodeEntry` tuple consisting of `[Node, Path]`.

Options: `{from?: Path, to?: Path, reverse?: boolean, pass?: (node: NodeEntry => boolean)}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.elements-root-node-options-greater-than-generator-less-than-elemententry-greater-than)

`Node.elements(root: Node, options?) => Generator<ElementEntry>`

Return a generator of all the element nodes inside a root node. Each iteration will return an `ElementEntry` tuple consisting of `[Element, Path]`. If the root node is an element, it will be included in the iteration as well.

Options: `{from?: Path, to?: Path, reverse?: boolean, pass?: (node: NodeEntry => boolean)}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.extractprops-node-node-greater-than-nodeprops)

`Node.extractProps(node: Node) => NodeProps`

Extract all properties from a Node except for its content-related fields (`children` for Element nodes and `text` for Text nodes).

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.first-root-node-path-path-greater-than-nodeentry)

`Node.first(root: Node, path: Path) => NodeEntry`

Get the first node entry in a root node from a `path`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.fragment-root-node-range-range-greater-than-descendant)

`Node.fragment(root: Node, range: Range) => Descendant[]`

Get the sliced fragment represented by the `range`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.get-root-node-path-path-greater-than-node)

`Node.get(root: Node, path: Path) => Node`

Get the descendant node referred to by a specific `path`. If the path is an empty array, get the root node itself.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.getif-root-node-path-path-greater-than-node-or-undefined)

`Node.getIf(root: Node, path: Path) => Node | undefined`

Get a descendant node at a specific path, returning `undefined` if the node does not exist. This is a safer alternative to `Node.get()` as it won't throw an error if the path is invalid.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.last-root-node-path-path-greater-than-nodeentry)

`Node.last(root: Node, path: Path) => NodeEntry`

Get the last node entry in a root node at a specific `path`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.leaf-root-node-path-path-greater-than-text)

`Node.leaf(root: Node, path: Path) => Text`

Get the node at a specific `path`, ensuring it's a leaf text node. If the node is not a leaf text node, throw an error.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.levels-root-node-path-path-options-greater-than-generator-less-than-nodeentry-greater-than)

`Node.levels(root: Node, path: Path, options?) => Generator<NodeEntry>`

Return a generator of the nodes in a branch of the tree, from a specific `path`. By default, the order is top-down, from the highest to the lowest node in the tree, but you can pass the `reverse: true` option to go bottom-up.

Options: `{reverse?: boolean}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.nodes-root-node-options-greater-than-generator-less-than-nodeentry-greater-than)

`Node.nodes(root: Node, options?) => Generator<NodeEntry>`

Return a generator of all the node entries of a root node. Each entry is returned as a `[Node, Path]` tuple, with the path referring to the node's position inside the root node.

Options: `{from?: Path, to?: Path, reverse?: boolean, pass?: (node: NodeEntry => boolean)}`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.parent-root-node-path-path-greater-than-ancestor)

`Node.parent(root: Node, path: Path) => Ancestor`

Get the parent of a node at a specific `path`.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#text-methods)

Text methods

Methods related to Text.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.string-root-node-greater-than-string)

`Node.string(root: Node) => string`

Get the concatenated text string of a node's content. Note that this will not include spaces or line breaks between block nodes. This is not intended as a user-facing string, but as a string for performing offset-related computations for a node.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.texts-root-node-options-greater-than-generator-less-than-nodeentry-less-than-text-greater-than)

`Node.texts(root: Node, options?) => Generator<NodeEntry<Text>>`

Return a generator of all leaf text nodes in a root node.

Options: `{from?: Path, to?: Path, reverse?: boolean, pass?: (node: NodeEntry => boolean)}`

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#check-methods)

Check methods

Methods used to check some attribute of a Node.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.has-root-node-path-path-greater-than-boolean)

`Node.has(root: Node, path: Path) => boolean`

Check if a descendant node exists at a specific `path`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.isnode-value-any-greater-than-value-is-node)

`Node.isNode(value: any) => value is Node`

Check if a `value` implements the `Node` interface.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.isnodelist-value-any-greater-than-value-is-node)

`Node.isNodeList(value: any) => value is Node[]`

Check if a `value` is a list of `Node` objects.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node#node.matches-root-node-props-partial-less-than-node-greater-than-greater-than-boolean)

`Node.matches(root: Node, props: Partial<Node>) => boolean`

Check if a node matches a set of `props`.

[PreviousElementchevron-left](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/element)
[NextNodeEntrychevron-right](https://docs.slatejs.org/api/nodes/node-entry)

Copy

    // For an Element node
    const element = {
      type: 'paragraph',
      align: 'center',
      children: [{ text: 'Try it out for yourself!' }],
    }
    const props = Node.extractProps(element)
    // Returns: { type: 'paragraph', align: "center" }
    
    // For a Text node
    const text = { text: 'Hello', bold: true }
    const props = Node.extractProps(text)
    // Returns: { bold: true }

    const node = Node.getIf(root, [0, 1])
    if (node) {
      // node exists at path [0, 1]
    } else {
      // no node exists at path [0, 1]
    }

# Resources | Slate

A few resources that are helpful for building with Slate.

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/general/resources#libraries)

Libraries


------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These libraries are helpful when developing with Slate:

*   [`is-hotkey`arrow-up-right](https://github.com/ianstormtaylor/is-hotkey)
     is a simple way to check whether an `onKeyDown` handler should fire for a given hotkey, handling cross-platform concerns like cmd vs. ctrl keys for you automatically.
    

[hashtag](https://docs.slatejs.org/general/resources#extensions-and-plugins)

Extensions and Plugins


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These extensions and plugins add additional features and capabilities to Slate:

*   [@liveblocks/yjsarrow-up-right](https://liveblocks.io/docs/api-reference/liveblocks-yjs)
     A fully-hosted WebSocket infrastructure and persisted data store for Yjs documents
    
*   [Platearrow-up-right](https://github.com/udecode/plate)
     Rich text editor plugin system for Slate & React
    
*   [`slate-angular`arrow-up-right](https://github.com/worktile/slate-angular)
     Angular-based view layer, which is a useful supplement to Slate for building a rich text editor using Angular.
    
*   [`slate-yjs`arrow-up-right](https://github.com/BitPhinix/slate-yjs/)
     Collaborative editing utilities for Slate leveraging Yjs
    
*   [`slate-collaborative`arrow-up-right](https://github.com/cudr/slate-collaborative)
     Collaborative editing utilities for Slate leveraging Automerge
    
*   [`slate-vue3`arrow-up-right](https://github.com/Guan-Erjia/slate-vue3)
     Which is a useful supplement to Slate for building a rich text editor using Vue3, integrated all functions in an npm package
